    "prepare-dataset": {
      "template": "## Arguments\n\n- `$FILE` : path to the source file (e.g. `data/products.csv`, `data/clients.json`)\n- `$GOAL` : one sentence describing what the model should be able to do after fine-tuning (e.g. \"answer questions about our product catalogue in English\")\n\n## Steps\n\n### 1. Analyse the source file\n\nStart by reading and analysing `$FILE`:\n\n- Detect the format (CSV, JSON, JSONL, TSV, Parquet) and the delimiter if CSV\n- Identify all available fields/columns and their types (string, number, bool...)\n- Count the total number of rows\n- Measure the missing value rate per field\n- Display 3 sample rows to understand the structure\n- Identify rich fields (few missing values, varied content) vs. sparse fields (>50% empty, constant values)\n\n### 2. Propose a strategy\n\nBased on `$GOAL` and the analysis, propose:\n\n- Which fields to use and why (exclude fields that are too empty or irrelevant)\n- How many Q&A pairs per source row can be generated (~5 to 30 depending on richness)\n- Estimated final dataset size (rows x average examples)\n- If the dataset is too small (<100 final examples): suggest an augmentation strategy (phrasing variants, synthetic data)\n- Recommended filter (e.g. \"keep only rows where field X is filled\")\n\n**Wait for validation before generating the script.**\n\n### 3. Generate `scripts/dataset/<n>.py`\n\nGenerate a Python script that **inherits from `BaseDatasetPreparer`** (see `scripts/dataset/base.py`), with the following structure:\n\n**Header and imports**\n\n```python\n\"\"\"\nscripts/dataset/<n>.py\n──────────────────────────\nShort description of what this script does.\nSource : $FILE\nGoal   : $GOAL\n\nUsage :\n    uv run sg-<n> --input data/<n>.csv --stats\n    uv run <n>-quality\n\"\"\"\n```\n\n**Lookup tables** (if codes or abbreviations are present in the data) Generate Python dicts to translate them into human-readable text (e.g. country codes -> names).\n\n**Class `<n>Preparer(BaseDatasetPreparer)`** with two methods:\n\n`generate_examples(self, row: dict) -> list[dict]`\n\n- Takes one source row as input\n- Returns a list of dicts `{\"instruction\": str, \"input\": str, \"output\": str}`\n- Generates between 5 and 30 Q&A pairs per row depending on data richness\n- Covers each important fact under 2-3 different phrasings (e.g. \"What is X of Y?\" / \"Give me X for Y.\" / \"What is the X value of Y?\")\n- Includes at least one \"full record\" question that aggregates all fields\n- Handles missing fields gracefully (`if field:` before using)\n- All questions and answers match the language implied by `$GOAL`\n\n`filter_rows(self, rows: list[dict], mode: str) -> list[dict]`\n\n- mode `quality`: only rows with essential fields filled (determined by the analysis)\n- mode `full`: all rows\n\n**`main()` function** with argparse:\n\n```\n--input         path to the source file\n--output        output prefix without extension (default: dataset/<n>)\n--mode          full | quality  (default: quality)\n--train-ratio   float 0.0-1.0  (default: 0.9)\n--seed          int             (default: 42)\n--stats         flag -- display random sample examples\n```\n\nThe `main()` function instantiates the preparer and calls `self.build(...)`. Do **not** re-implement the build pipeline -- it is provided by `BaseDatasetPreparer`.\n\n### 4. Update pyproject.toml\n\nAfter creating the script, automatically add two entries to `pyproject.toml`:\n\nIn `[project.scripts]`:\n\n```toml\nsg-<n> = \"scripts.dataset.<n>:main\"\n```\n\nIn `[tool.uv.scripts]`:\n\n```toml\n<n>-quality  = \"python scripts/dataset/<n>.py --mode quality --stats\"\n<n>-full     = \"python scripts/dataset/<n>.py --mode full --stats\"\n<n>-validate = \"python scripts/dataset/validate.py dataset/<n>_train.jsonl\"\n```\n\n### 5. Final validation\n\n- Run `uv run python scripts/dataset/<n>.py --mode quality --stats` to verify the script runs without errors\n- Display the generation summary (number of examples, output files)\n- Display 3 generated Q&A examples for visual validation\n- Confirm that `dataset/<n>_train.jsonl` and `dataset/<n>_test.jsonl` exist\n\n## Quality rules for the generated script\n\n- `generate_examples` and `filter_rows` must be **pure functions** -- no I/O, no side effects\n- Type hints on all public methods and functions\n- Docstring on every method\n- Missing field handling without crash (`row.get(\"field\", \"\").strip()`)\n- Fixed `random.seed` for reproducibility (handled by `BaseDatasetPreparer.build`)\n- snake_case naming, compliant with the project's Ruff config\n- Compatible with both `uv run` and direct `python` invocation\n\n## Expected JSONL output format\n\nEach line of the produced file must be:\n\n```json\n{\n  \"input\": \"\",\n  \"instruction\": \"Natural language question?\",\n  \"output\": \"Factual answer.\"\n}\n```\n\nThe `input` field is always an empty string for Q&A datasets. The `instruction` field must never exceed 200 characters. The `output` field may be multi-line for full-record questions.\n\n## Usage examples\n\n```\n/prepare-dataset data/products.csv \"answer questions about our product catalogue\"\n/prepare-dataset data/clients.json \"classify clients by B2B segment and answer CRM questions\"\n/prepare-dataset data/transactions.csv \"detect suspicious transactions and explain why\"\n/prepare-dataset data/airports.csv \"answer questions about airports worldwide in French\"\n```",
      "description": "Analyse a raw data file (CSV, JSON, JSONL, TSV, Parquet) and generate a complete Python script `scripts/dataset/<n>.py` that inherits from `BaseDatasetPreparer` and transforms the file into a JSONL dataset ready for fine-tuning with Unsloth.",

diff, Layer 2 = tool call [optional], Layer 3 = cache check)\n- **Comprehensive reporting**: Documents every plugin's repair status and findings\n\n## Safety\n\n- **Default is dry-run**: Without `--apply`, only reports what would be done\n- **Disk safety**: Refuses to proceed if free space < 500 MB\n- **OS-aware**: Silently skips incompatible plugins (doesn't remove them from config)\n-       "template": "# Datadog CLI Quick Reference\n\n## Commands Overview\n\n| Command         | Purpose                            |\n| --------------- | ---------------------------------- |\n| `logs search`   | Search and filter logs             |\n| `logs agg`      | Aggregate logs by facet            |\n| `logs tail`     | Stream logs in real-time           |\n| `logs trace`    | Find logs for a trace ID           |\n| `logs context`  | Get logs around a timestamp        |\n| `logs patterns` | Group similar log messages         |\n| `logs compare`  | Compare current vs previous period |\n| `logs multi`    | Run multiple queries in parallel   |\n| `metrics query` | Query timeseries metrics           |\n| `errors`        | Quick error summary                |\n| `services`      | List services with log activity    |\n\n## Log Search\n\n```bash\ndatadog logs search --query \"<query>\" --from <time> [--limit <n>] [--pretty]\n```\n\n**Examples:**\n\n```bash\n# All errors in last hour\ndatadog logs search --query \"status:error\" --from 1h --pretty\n\n# Errors for a specific service\ndatadog logs search --query \"service:api status:error\" --from 1h --pretty\n\n# HTTP 500 errors\ndatadog logs search --query \"@http.status_code:500\" --from 30m --pretty\n\n# Errors containing specific text\ndatadog logs search --query \"status:error connection refused\" --from 1h --pretty\n\n# Exclude certain services\ndatadog logs search --query \"status:error -service:healthcheck\" --from 1h --pretty\n```\n\n## Log Aggregation\n\n```bash\ndatadog logs agg --query \"<query>\" --facet <facet> --from <time> [--pretty]\n```\n\n**Common facets:** `status`, `service`, `host`, `@http.status_code`, `@error.kind`, `@http.method`\n\n**Examples:**\n\n```bash\n# Count logs by status level\ndatadog logs agg --query \"*\" --facet status --from 1h --pretty\n\n# Errors by service\ndatadog logs agg --query \"status:error\" --facet service --from 24h --pretty\n\n# Requests by HTTP status code\ndatadog logs agg --query \"service:api\" --facet @http.status_code --from 1h --pretty\n\n# Errors by error type\ndatadog logs agg --query \"status:error\" --facet @error.kind --from 6h --pretty\n```\n\n## Live Tail (Real-time)\n\n```bash\ndatadog logs tail --query \"<query>\" [--interval <seconds>] [--pretty]\n```\n\n**Examples:**\n\n```bash\n# Stream all errors\ndatadog logs tail --query \"status:error\" --pretty\n\n# Watch specific service\ndatadog logs tail --query \"service:payment-api\" --pretty\n\n# Watch with custom poll interval\ndatadog logs tail --query \"status:error\" --interval 5 --pretty\n```\n\n## Trace Correlation\n\n```bash\ndatadog logs trace --id \"<trace-id>\" [--from <time>] [--pretty]\n```\n\n**Example:**\n\n```bash\ndatadog logs trace --id \"abc123def456789\" --from 24h --pretty\n```\n\n## Log Context\n\nGet logs before/after a specific timestamp to understand what happened.\n\n```bash\ndatadog logs context --timestamp \"<iso-timestamp>\" [--service <svc>] [--before <time>] [--after <time>] [--pretty]\n```\n\n**Examples:**\n\n```bash\n# 5 minutes before/after a timestamp\ndatadog logs context --timestamp \"2024-01-15T10:30:00Z\" --pretty\n\n# Focused on one service\ndatadog logs context --timestamp \"2024-01-15T10:30:00Z\" --service api --before 10m --after 5m --pretty\n```\n\n## Error Summary\n\n```bash\ndatadog errors [--from <time>] [--service <svc>] [--pretty]\n```\n\n**Examples:**\n\n```bash\n# All errors in last hour\ndatadog errors --from 1h --pretty\n\n# Errors for specific service\ndatadog errors --service payment-api --from 24h --pretty\n```\n\n## Log Patterns\n\nGroup similar messages (replaces UUIDs, numbers, IPs with placeholders).\n\n```bash\ndatadog logs patterns --query \"<query>\" --from <time> [--limit <n>] [--pretty]\n```\n\n**Examples:**\n\n```bash\n# Find error patterns\ndatadog logs patterns --query \"status:error\" --from 1h --pretty\n\n# Patterns for a service\ndatadog logs patterns --query \"service:api\" --from 6h --limit 500 --pretty\n```\n\n## Period Comparison\n\nCompare log counts: current period vs previous period.\n\n```bash\ndatadog logs compare --query \"<query>\" --period <time> [--pretty]\n```\n\n**Examples:**\n\n```bash\n# Are errors increasing? Compare last hour to hour before\ndatadog logs compare --query \"status:error\" --period 1h --pretty\n\n# Compare 500 errors over 6 hour periods\ndatadog logs compare --query \"@http.status_code:500\" --period 6h --pretty\n```\n\n## Multiple Queries\n\nRun several queries in parallel.\n\n```bash\ndatadog logs multi --queries \"name1:query1,name2:query2\" --from <time> [--pretty]\n```\n\n**Examples:**\n\n```bash\n# Errors vs warnings\ndatadog logs multi --queries \"errors:status:error,warnings:status:warn\" --from 1h --pretty\n\n# Multiple services\ndatadog logs multi --queries \"api:service:api,db:service:database,cache:service:redis\" --from 1h --pretty\n```\n\n## Service Discovery\n\n```bash\ndatadog services --from <time> [--pretty]\n```\n\n**Example:**\n\n```bash\ndatadog services --from 24h --pretty\n```\n\n## Metrics Query\n\n```bash\ndatadog metrics query --query \"<aggregation>:<metric>{<tags>}\" --from <time> [--pretty]\n```\n\n**Aggregations:** `avg`, `sum`, `min`, `max`, `count`\n\n**Examples:**\n\n```bash\n# CPU usage across all hosts\ndatadog metrics query --query \"avg:system.cpu.user{*}\" --from 1h --pretty\n\n# CPU for specific service\ndatadog metrics query --query \"avg:system.cpu.user{service:api}\" --from 1h --pretty\n\n# Memory usage\ndatadog metrics query --query \"avg:system.mem.used{*}\" --from 1h --pretty\n\n# Request count\ndatadog metrics query --query \"sum:trace.http.request.hits{service:api}.as_count()\" --from 1h --pretty\n\n# Error rate\ndatadog metrics query --query \"sum:trace.http.request.errors{service:api}.as_count()\" --from 1h --pretty\n```\n\n## Query Syntax\n\n| Operator | Example | Description |\n| --- | --- | --- |\n| implicit AND | `service:api status:error` | Both conditions |\n| `OR` | `status:error OR status:warn` | Either condition |\n| `-` (NOT) | `-service:healthcheck` | Exclude matches |\n| `*` wildcard | `service:api-*` | Prefix/suffix match |\n| `>=` `<=` `>` `<` | `@http.status_code:>=400` | Numeric comparison |\n| `[TO]` range | `@duration:[1000 TO 5000]` | Numeric range |\n| `\"\"` exact | `\"connection refused\"` | Exact phrase |\n\n## Common Log Attributes\n\n| Attribute           | Description                                 |\n| ------------------- | ------------------------------------------- |\n| `status`            | Log level: `error`, `warn`, `info`, `debug` |\n| `service`           | Service name                                |\n| `host`              | Hostname                                    |\n| `@http.status_code` | HTTP response code                          |\n| `@http.method`      | GET, POST, PUT, DELETE, etc.                |\n| `@http.url`         | Request URL                                 |\n| `@error.kind`       | Error type/class                            |\n| `@error.message`    | Error message                               |\n| `@trace_id`         | Distributed trace ID                        |\n| `@duration`         | Request duration (nanoseconds)              |\n\n## Time Formats\n\n- Relative: `30m`, `1h`, `6h`, `24h`, `7d`\n- ISO 8601: `2024-01-15T10:30:00Z`\n\n## Global Flags\n\n| Flag | Description |\n| --- | --- |\n| `--pretty` | Human-readable colored output |\n| `--output <file>` | Export results to JSON file |\n| `--site <site>` | Datadog site (e.g., `datadoghq.eu`, `us5.datadoghq.com`) |\n\n## Common Workflows\n\n### Incident Triage\n\n```bash\ndatadog errors --from 1h --pretty                                    # Overview\ndatadog logs compare --query \"status:error\" --period 1h --pretty     # Is this new?\ndatadog logs patterns --query \"status:error\" --from 1h --pretty      # What patterns?\ndatadog logs search --query \"status:error service:api\" --from 1h --pretty  # Drill down\ndatadog logs trace --id \"TRACE_ID\" --pretty                          # Follow trace\n```\n\n### Real-time Monitoring\n\n```bash\ndatadog logs tail --query \"status:error\" --pretty\n```\n\n### Export for Analysis\n\n```bash\ndatadog logs search --query \"status:error\" --from 24h --limit 1000 --output errors.json\n```",

      "template": "# Draft Professional Email\n\nGenerate a professional, well-structured email using communication best practices for software developers.\n\n## Arguments\n\n`$ARGUMENTS` - Optional context, topic, or existing draft to refine\n\n## Workflow\n\n### Step 1: Gather Context\n\nIf `$ARGUMENTS` is empty or insufficient, use AskUserQuestion to gather:\n\n**Question 1: Recipient Type** (header: \"Audience\")\n\n- Technical peer (developer, engineer)\n- Non-technical stakeholder (PM, executive, customer)\n- Cross-functional team (mixed audience)\n- Manager or leadership\n\n**Question 2: Email Purpose** (header: \"Purpose\")\n\n- Status update or progress report\n- Request (review, approval, resources)\n- Information sharing (FYI, announcement)\n- Escalation or raising concern\n- Following up on prior conversation\n\n**Question 3: Urgency** (header: \"Urgency\")\n\n- Urgent - needs response today\n- Standard - within 1-2 days\n- Low priority - for awareness only\n\n### Step 2: Apply Communication Framework\n\nUse the **What-Why-How** structure:\n\n1. **WHAT** (Opening - 1-2 sentences)\n   - Lead with the key message or request\n   - State the purpose immediately\n   - No throat-clearing (\"I hope this email finds you well...\")\n\n2. **WHY** (Context - 2-3 sentences)\n   - Provide necessary background\n   - Explain relevance to the recipient\n   - Include only essential context\n\n3. **HOW** (Action - clear next steps)\n   - Specific call-to-action\n   - Clear deadline if applicable\n   - Who needs to do what\n\n### Step 3: Apply Email Best Practices\n\n**Subject Line:**\n\n- Specific and scannable (5-8 words ideal)\n- Include action needed: \"[Action Required]\", \"[FYI]\", \"[Decision Needed]\"\n- Include deadline if urgent: \"[Due Friday]\"\n\n**Body Structure:**\n\n- Bullets for multiple points (3-5 max)\n- Bold key information\n- One topic per email\n- Short paragraphs (2-3 sentences max)\n\n**Tone Calibration by Audience:**\n\n| Audience | Tone | Jargon Level |\n| --- | --- | --- |\n| Technical peer | Direct, precise | High (use technical terms) |\n| Non-technical | Business-focused | Low (translate jargon) |\n| Cross-functional | Balanced | Medium (explain as needed) |\n| Leadership | Concise, impact-focused | Low (focus on outcomes) |\n\n### Step 4: Generate Draft\n\nProduce a complete email with:\n\n```markdown\n## Email Draft\n\n**Subject:** [Clear, specific subject line]\n\n---\n\n[Opening - WHAT: Key message/request]\n\n[Context - WHY: Background and relevance]\n\n[Body - Details as needed, use bullets for lists]\n\n[Closing - HOW: Clear call-to-action]\n\n[Sign-off]\n```\n\n### Step 5: Offer Refinements\n\nAfter presenting the draft, offer:\n\n1. **Tone adjustment** - Make more/less formal\n2. **Length adjustment** - Expand or condense\n3. **Jargon translation** - Adjust technical language level\n4. **Format change** - Different structure for different medium (Slack, Teams)\n\n## Example Usage\n\n```bash\n# With context\n/soft-skills:draft-email Need to ask team lead for deadline extension on API migration\n\n# Refine existing draft\n/soft-skills:draft-email \"Hi team, wanted to let you know about the deployment...\"\n\n# Start fresh\n/soft-skills:draft-email\n```\n\n## Output\n\nPresent the draft in a clear format showing:\n\n1. **Subject line** with rationale\n2. **Email body** with WHAT/WHY/HOW sections labeled\n3. **Refinement options** for iteration\n\n## Anti-Patterns to Avoid\n\n- Generic subjects (\"Quick question\", \"Update\", \"FYI\")\n- Burying the request at the end\n- Wall of text without structure\n- Missing clear call-to-action\n- Over-apologizing or excessive hedging\n- CC'ing unnecessarily",

    "commit": {
      "template": "# Commit Command\n\nYou are an AI agent that helps create well-formatted git commits with conventional commit messages and emoji icons, follow these instructions exactly. Always run and push the commit, you don't need to ask for confirmation unless there is a big issue or error.\n\nPrefer to explain **WHY** something was done from an end user perspective instead of **WHAT** was done.\n\n## Instructions for Agent\n\nWhen the user runs this command, execute the following workflow:\n\n1. **Check command mode**:\n   - If user you have $ARGUMENTS which is simple, skip to step 3\n2. **Run pre-commit validation**:\n   - Execute `pre-commit run -a` and report any issues\n   - If fails, ask user if they want to proceed anyway or fix issues first\n3. **Analyze git status**:\n   - Run `git status --porcelain` to check for changes\n   - If no files are staged, run `git add .` to stage all modified files\n   - If files are already staged, proceed with only those files\n4. **Analyze the changes**:\n   - Run `git diff --cached` to see what will be committed\n   - Analyze the diff to determine the primary change type (feat, fix, docs, etc.)\n   - Identify the main scope and purpose of the changes\n5. **Generate commit message**:\n   - Choose appropriate emoji and type from the reference below\n   - Create message following format: `<emoji> <type>: <description>`\n   - Keep description concise, clear, and in imperative mood\n   - Show the proposed message to user for confirmation\n6. **Execute the commit**:\n   - Run `git commit -m \"<generated message>\"`\n   - Display the commit hash and confirm success\n   - Provide brief summary of what was committed\n\n## Commit Message Guidelines\n\nWhen generating commit messages, follow these rules:\n\n- **Atomic commits**: Each commit should contain related changes that serve a single purpose\n- **Imperative mood**: Write as commands (e.g., \"add feature\" not \"added feature\")\n- **Concise first line**: Keep under 72 characters\n- **Conventional format**: Use `<emoji> <type>: <description>` where type is one of:\n  - `feat`: A new feature\n  - `fix`: A bug fix\n  - `docs`: Documentation changes\n  - `style`: Code style changes (formatting, etc.)\n  - `refactor`: Code changes that neither fix bugs nor add features\n  - `perf`: Performance improvements\n  - `test`: Adding or fixing tests\n  - `chore`: Changes to the build process, tools, etc.\n- **Present tense, imperative mood**: Write commit messages as commands (e.g., \"add feature\" not \"added feature\")\n- **Concise first line**: Keep the first line under 72 characters\n- **Emoji**: Each commit type is paired with an appropriate emoji:\n  - ✨ `feat`: New feature\n  - 🐛 `fix`: Bug fix\n  - 📝 `docs`: Documentation\n  - 💄 `style`: Formatting/style\n  - ♻️ `refactor`: Code refactoring\n  - ⚡️ `perf`: Performance improvements\n  - ✅ `test`: Tests\n  - 🔧 `chore`: Tooling, configuration\n  - 🚀 `ci`: CI/CD improvements\n  - 🗑️ `revert`: Reverting changes\n  - 🧪 `test`: Add a failing test\n  - 🚨 `fix`: Fix compiler/linter warnings\n  - 🔒️ `fix`: Fix security issues\n  - 👥 `chore`: Add or update contributors\n  - 🚚 `refactor`: Move or rename resources\n  - 🏗️ `refactor`: Make architectural changes\n  - 🔀 `chore`: Merge branches\n  - 📦️ `chore`: Add or update compiled files or packages\n  - ➕ `chore`: Add a dependency\n  - ➖ `chore`: Remove a dependency\n  - 🌱 `chore`: Add or update seed files\n  - 🧑‍💻 `chore`: Improve developer experience\n  - 🧵 `feat`: Add or update code related to multithreading or concurrency\n  - 🔍️ `feat`: Improve SEO\n  - 🏷️ `feat`: Add or update types\n  - 💬 `feat`: Add or update text and literals\n  - 🌐 `feat`: Internationalization and localization\n  - 👔 `feat`: Add or update business logic\n  - 📱 `feat`: Work on responsive design\n  - 🚸 `feat`: Improve user experience / usability\n  - 🩹 `fix`: Simple fix for a non-critical issue\n  - 🥅 `fix`: Catch errors\n  - 👽️ `fix`: Update code due to external API changes\n  - 🔥 `fix`: Remove code or files\n  - 🎨 `style`: Improve structure/format of the code\n  - 🚑️ `fix`: Critical hotfix\n  - 🎉 `chore`: Begin a project\n  - 🔖 `chore`: Release/Version tags\n  - 🚧 `wip`: Work in progress\n  - 💚 `fix`: Fix CI build\n  - 📌 `chore`: Pin dependencies to specific versions\n  - 👷 `ci`: Add or update CI build system\n  - 📈 `feat`: Add or update analytics or tracking code\n  - ✏️ `fix`: Fix typos\n  - ⏪️ `revert`: Revert changes\n  - 📄 `chore`: Add or update license\n  - 💥 `feat`: Introduce breaking `scripts/ts/**/*.ts`\n\n### 5.3 Script Enhancement Pattern\n\n**Before (Shell with logic - BAD):**\n\n```bash\n#!/bin/bash\n# BAD - logic in shell\nfor file in $(find . -name \"*.ts\"); do\n  echo \"Processing $file\"\ndone\n```\n\n**After (Shell = orchestrator - GOOD):**\n\n```bash\n#!/bin/bash\n# GOOD - orchestrator only\nbunx tsx scripts/ts/utils/process-files.ts \"$@\"\n```\n\n```typescript\n// scripts/ts/utils/process-files.ts\nimport { Project } from \"ts-morph\";\nimport { parseArgs } from \"util\";\n\ninterface Options {\n  dryRun: boolean;\n  verbose: boolean;\n}\n\nexport async function processFiles(args: string[]): Promise<void> {\n  const options = parseArgs({\n    options: {\n      \"dry-run\": { type: \"boolean\", default: false },\n      verbose: { type: \"boolean\", default: false }\n    },\n    args\n  });\n\n  const project = new Project({\n    tsConfigFilePath: \"./tsconfig.json\"\n  });\n  const sourceFiles = project.getSourceFiles(\"**/*.ts\");\n\n  if (options.values.dryRun) {\n    console.log(\n      \"[DRY RUN] Would process:\",\n      sourceFiles.length,\n      \"files\"\n    );\n    return;\n  }\n\n  // Process files...\n}\n```\n\n### 5.4 Add Dry-Run to All Mutation Scripts\n\n```typescript\n// All mutation scripts must support --dry-run\nconst isDryRun = process.argv.includes(\"--dry-run\");\n\nif (isDryRun) {\n  console.log(\"[DRY RUN] Changes that would be made:\");\n  // Log what would change without making changes\n} else {\n  // Actually make the changes\n}\n```\n\n### 5.5 Script Inventory Documentation\n\nUpdate `docs/scripts.md` with:\n\n| Script | Type | Purpose | Flags |\n| --- | --- | --- | --- |\n| `scripts/db:push` | Orchestrator | Push DB schema | None |\n| `scripts/db:seed` | Orchestrator | Seed test data | `--reset` |\n| `scripts/verify-rules` | Logic | AST policy check | `--verbose` |\n| `scripts/ts/deploy/deploy.ts` | Logic | Deploy logic | `--dry-run` |\n\n---\n\n## PHASE 5 EXTRAS: CREATE init-enhanced.md\n\n### File: `.opencode/commands/init-enhanced.md`\n\n````markdown\n---\ncategory: initialization\ndescription: requirements\n\nCo-authored-by: Claude <copilot@opencode>\"\n```\n\n---\n\n## Self-Review Checklist\n\nBefore dispatch:\n\n- [ ] All 4 tasks cover Phase 0 scope (custom-components, app-pages, test-context, scripts)\n- [ ] Each task produces a concrete markdown file or enhancement\n- [ ] Each step includes exact file paths, commands, expected output\n- [ ] No placeholders (\"TBD\", \"similar to\", \"add validation\")\n- [ ] Tasks can execute independently (no cross-task dependencies)\n- [ ] Commits are atomic and follow convention\n- [ ] Execution is subagent-driven-development (fresh subagent per task)\n\n---\n\n## Execution Strategy\n\nThis plan is designed for **subagent-driven development** with:\n\n- **Fresh subagent per task** (Task 0.1, 0.2, 0.3, 0.4)\n- **Two-stage review per task:** (1) Spec compliance (docs match code), (2) Commit quality\n- **Isolated context:** Each subagent has its own session; no history bleed\n- **Two-minute tasks:** Most steps take 2–5 minutes per-step, allowing rapid iteration\n\n**Total Phase 0 execution time:** ~2–3 hours (with review gates)\n\nAfter Task 0.4 completion, Phase 1 (Dead-Code Removal) can proceed with high-fidelity documentation as reference."

      "template": "GOAL: You are creating a handoff message to continue work in a new session.\n\n<context>\nWhen an AI assistant starts a fresh session, it spends significant time exploring the codebase—grepping, reading files, searching—before it can begin actual work. This \"file archaeology\" is wasteful when the previous session already discovered what matters.\n\nA good handoff frontloads everything the next session needs so it can start implementing immediately.\n</context>\n\n<instructions>\nAnalyze this conversation and extract what matters for continuing the work.\n\n1. Identify all relevant files that should be loaded into the next session's context\n\n   Include files that will be edited, dependencies being touched, relevant tests, configs, and key reference docs. Be generous—the cost of an extra file is low; missing a critical one means another archaeology dig. Target 8-15 files, up to 20 for complex work.\n\n2. Draft the context and goal description\n\n   Describe what we're working on and provide whatever context helps continue the work. Structure it based on what fits the conversation—could be tasks, findings, a simple paragraph, or detailed steps.\n\n   Preserve: decisions, constraints, user preferences, technical patterns.\n\n   Exclude: conversation back-and-forth, dead ends, meta-commentary.\n\nThe user controls what context matters. If they mentioned something to preserve, include it—trust their judgment about their workflow.\n</instructions>\n\n<user_input>\nThis is what the next session should focus on. Use it to shape your handoff's direction—don't investigate or search, just incorporate the intent into your context and goals.\n\nIf empty, capture a natural continuation of the current conversation's direction.\n\nUSER: $ARGUMENTS\n</user_input>\n\n---\n\nAfter generating the handoff message, IMMEDIATELY call handoff_session with your prompt and files:\n`handoff_session(prompt=\"...\", files=[\"src/foo.ts\", \"src/bar.ts\", ...])`"
